Genetic differentiation and biogeographic breaks

Goals

What follows is our workflow for estimating genetic distance and differentiation among East Asian and Philippine Zosterops populations and across biogeographic breaks based on single nucleotide polymorphism (SNP) data from our double digest restriction-site associated DNA (ddRAD) library.

Getting started

We are using R version 4.4.2, RStudio version 2024.09.1 for the analysis. Quarto version 1.6.39 for Mac OS was used to document the workflow. Set the working directory in RStudio to one where the vcf file for the SNPs and a text file defining the population for each sample are available.

Packages

Set the working directory to one where the SNP data file zost.filtered.snps.vcf and the taxon/population designation file ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt are both accessible. Conducting the distance and Fst analysis on these data and generating the associated figures and maps requires the following R packages.

  • logr (Bosak 2024) Optional if you wish to create a log file for the analysis.

  • vcfR (Knaus and Grünwald 2017)

  • SNPfiltR (DeRaad 2023)

  • ggplot2 (Wickham 2016)

  • adegenet (Jombart 2008)

  • StAMPP (Pembleton, Cogan, and Forster 2013)

  • maps (Becker, Minka, and Deckmyn. 2024)

  • sf (Pebesma and Bivand 2023)

  • dartR.base (Gruber et al. 2018)

Restart R in the Session/Restart R drop-down in R Studio and create a log file for the analysis (optional).

library(logr)
Loading required package: common
log_open(file_name = "ZosteropsDistanceFST.log")
[1] "./log/ZosteropsDistanceFST.log"

After making sure they are installed load the libraries for each required package.

Data files

This analysis requires the filtered variant call format (VCF) file titled zost.filtered.snps.vcf. Additionally the population of origin and/or taxon assignment will need to be defined for each sample. Taxon and population data for this analysis is in the file titled ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt. In this file populations are defined in reference to the following combinations of (mostly) allopatric taxa and biogeographic regions. A second taxon assignment file was created assigning individual samples to mostly species designation or more broad allopatric groups within species. That file is titled ZosteropsSPECIES.txt. A detailed description of the assignments in each file is shown below. For discussions of biogeographic breaks in Japan and the Ryukyu Islands see Komaki 2021 (Komaki 2021) and McKay 2012 (McKay 2011).

Population (island and island group) assignments.

Assignment file ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt

  • Zosterops japonicus

    • japonicusKOREA The Korean Peninsula and adjacent islands of the South China Sea and Korean and Tsushima Straits.

    • japonicusJAPAN The main islands of the Japanese archipelago including Hokkaido, Honshu, Shikoku, and Kyushu.

    • japonicusRYUKYUn The northern Ryukyu islands of the Osumi group including Yakushima and Tanegashima. Populations with this designation are those in the broader Ryukyu archipelago but north of the biogeographic break known as Watse’s Line.

    • japonicusRYUKYUc The central Ryukyu islands including Amami and Okinawa and their adjacent islands.

    • japonicusRYUKYUs The southern-most Ryukyu islands of the Sakishima group including the Miyako Islands, Yaeyama Islands, and Yonaguni island.

    • japonicusIZU Populations of the Z. japonicus stejnegeri subspecies from the Izu Islands (including Niijima, Aogashima, Kozushima, and Miyake).

    • japonicusOGASAWARA Populations of the Z. japonicus alani subspecies in the Ogasawara (including Chichijima, Hahajima, Imotojima, Anejima, and Imotojima islands) and Volcano islands (Iwojima).

    • japonicusHAWAII Introduced population in the Hawaiian archipelago.

  • Zosterops meyeni

    • meyeniLANYU Lanyu island off the east coast of Taiwan.

    • meyeniBATAN The Batan Islands of the Philippines including Batan and Sabtang islands.

  • Zosterops montanus

    • montanusNORTH The Northern Philippine islands of Luzon and Mindoro.

    • montanusVISAYAS The Visayas region of the central Philippines including the main islands of Negros, Panay, Cebu, Bohol, Leyte, and Samar.

    • montanusMINDANAO The southern most islands of the Philippines including the island of Mindanao. Included with Z. montanus samples from Mindanao in this analysis is a Z. nigrorum sample (Zni14341). This sample originating from the island of Camiguin South off the northern coast of Mindanao was initially assigned to the Z. nigrorum subspecies catarmanensis but in this study was found to cluster strongly with the central and southern Philippine populations of Z. montanus in both Sanger sequencing and SNP datasets.

    • montanusPALAWAN Philippine Z. montanus population on the island of Palawan.

    • montanusINDONESIA Z. montanus populations of the Indonesian archipelago.

  • Zosterops simplex

    • simplexASIA All Z. simplex populations on either the island of Taiwan or on mainland continental Asia.

    • simplexNA Introduced Z. simplex populations in the southern California region of North America.

  • Additional outgroup taxa

    • erythropleurus Z. erythropleurus including samples originating in the breeding range in the Russian Far East and wintering individuals in Southeast Asia.

    • everetti Z. everetti in the Visayas and Southern Philippines.

    • nigrorum Z. nigrorum in the Visayas and Northern Philippines.

    • palpebrosus Z. palpebrosus samples from Vietnam.

Below are the taxon and population assignments in the file ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt with the column headers ID and POP.

Species assignments.

Assignment file ZosteropsSPECIES.txt

  • Zosterops japonicus

    • japonicus All populations of Z. japonicus in the main islands of Japan, Korean Peninsula, Ryukyu Islands, and Izu islands to Chichijima in the Ogasawara islands and the introduced Z. japonicus population in Hawaii.

    • japonicusOGASAWARA Populations of the Z. japonicus alani subspecies in the Ogasawara (including Hahajima, Imotojima, Anejima, and Imotojima islands) and Volcano islands (Iwojima) are the most divergent within the Z. japonicus taxon and are for exploratory purposes considered a separate taxon.

  • Zosterops meyeni

    • meyeni Populations on Lanyu island off the east coast fo Taiwan and the Batan Islands of the Philippines, including Batan and Sabtang islands.

  • Zosterops montanus

    • montanusNORTH The Northern Philippine islands of Luzon and Mindoro.

    • montanusSOUTH Philippine Z. montanus populations in the Visayas region of the central Philippines including the main islands of Negros, Panay, Cebu, Bohol, Leyte, and Samar and the southern most islands of the Philippines including the island of Mindanao. Included with Z. montanus samples from Mindanao in this analysis is a Z. nigrorum sample (Zni14341), see description in the previous section above.

    • montanusPALAWAN Philippine Z. montanus population on the island of Palawan.

    • montanusINDONESIA Z. montanus populations of the Indonesian archipelago.

  • Zosterops simplex

    • simplex All Z. simplex populations on either the island of Taiwan or on mainland continental Asia and introduced Z. simplex populations in the southern California region of North America.

  • Additional outgroup taxa

    • erythropleurus Z. erythropleurus including samples originating in the breeding range in the Russian Far East and wintering individuals in Southeast Asia.

    • everetti Z. everetti in the Visayas and Southern Philippines.

    • nigrorum Z. nigrorum in the Visayas and Northern Philippines.

    • palpebrosus Z. palpebrosus samples from Vietnam.

VCF file

Load the SNP data from the vcf file. Recall the ZosteropsVCF object to summarize the dataset. The ZosteropsVCF object should have 124 samples and 15,704 variants.

ZosteropsVCF <- read.vcfR("Data/VCF files/zost.filtered.snps.vcf")

Taxon and population assignments

Population (island and island group) assignments

Assign the taxon and population designations to the individual samples in the SNP dataset from the ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt file. Confirm that the IDs in the taxon/population file match the sample IDs in the VCF file.

sample.info <- read.table("Data/Taxon files/ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt", sep = "\t", header = TRUE)
sample.info <- sample.info[sample.info$ID %in% colnames(ZosteropsVCF@gt),]
table(sample.info$POP)

Species assignments

Create another set of assignments for mostly species level designations to the individual samples in the SNP dataset from the ZosteropsSPECIES.txt file. Confirm that the IDs in the taxon/population file match the sample IDs in the VCF file.

sample.species.info <- read.table("Data/Taxon files/ZosteropsSPECIES.txt", sep = "\t", header = TRUE) 
sample.species.info <- sample.species.info[sample.species.info$ID %in% colnames(ZosteropsVCF@gt),]
table(sample.species.info$POP)

Convert data to Genlight format

Convert the SNP dataset ZosteropsVCF object into a genlight object required for estimating distance and Fst in StAMMP and assign the correct taxa and populations to that object from the ZosteropsPOPS_distance.txt file (sample.info).

ZosteropsGEN <- vcfR2genlight(ZosteropsVCF)
ZosteropsGEN@pop <- as.factor(sample.info$POP)

Convert the SNP dataset ZosteropsVCF object into a genlight object and assign the correct species to that object from the ZosteropsSPECIES.txt assignments (sample.species.info). This genlight object (ZosteropsGENfdiff) will be used for an additional analysis of fixed differences at the species level.

ZosteropsGENfdiff <- vcfR2genlight(ZosteropsVCF)
ZosteropsGENfdiff@pop <- as.factor(sample.species.info$POP)

Fixed differences

Conduct a compliance check using the gl.compliance.check function in dartR on the ZosteropsGENfdiff genlight object. Use the gl.fixed.diff function to then count pairwise fixed SNP differences between the assigned species groups. Conduct the pairwise fixed differences analysis under the default parameters including alpha = 0.05 and a threshold value of 0.02 (delta = 0.02). Because these are the default parameters they do not appear as delineated in the command. Include in the fixed differences analysis a statistical test to estimate p-values associated with each pairwise comparison (test = TRUE).

Estimate Fst and Nei’s distance

Generate the Fst and Nei’s distance estimates from the Zosterops genlight object (ZosteropsGEN).

ZosteropsFST <- stamppFst(ZosteropsGEN, nboots = 100, percent = 95, nclusters = 4)
ZosteropsFSTmatrix <- ZosteropsFST$Fsts
ZosteropsFSTmatrix[upper.tri(ZosteropsFSTmatrix)] <- t(ZosteropsFSTmatrix)[upper.tri(ZosteropsFSTmatrix)]
ZosteropsFSTheat <- reshape::melt(ZosteropsFSTmatrix)
Warning in type.convert.default(X[[i]], ...): 'as.is' should be specified by
the caller; using TRUE
Warning in type.convert.default(X[[i]], ...): 'as.is' should be specified by
the caller; using TRUE
ZosteropsNeiDmatrix <- stamppNeisD(ZosteropsGEN, pop = TRUE)
ZosteropsNeiDmatrix[upper.tri(ZosteropsNeiDmatrix)] <- t(ZosteropsNeiDmatrix)[upper.tri(ZosteropsNeiDmatrix)]
ZosteropsNeiDheat <- reshape::melt(ZosteropsNeiDmatrix)
Warning in type.convert.default(X[[i]], ...): 'as.is' should be specified by
the caller; using TRUE

Pairwise Fst heatmap

Create a heatmap of the pairwise Fst estimates for each combination of taxa/populations.

ggplot(data = ZosteropsFSTheat, aes(x = X1, y = X2, fill = value))+
  geom_tile()+
  geom_text(data = ZosteropsFSTheat, aes(label = round(value, 2)))+
  theme_minimal()+
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "white", high = "red", space = "Lab", name = "Fst")+
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1), axis.text.y = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))

Create a heatmap of the pairwise Fst measurements for each combination of taxa/populations but this time reorganize so that populations within the same taxon are kept together and they are ordered based on genetic similarity.

# Define the desired order for the axes
ZosteropsFST_reorder <- c("japonicusJAPAN", "japonicusKOREA", "japonicusRYUKYUn", "japonicusRYUKYUc", "japonicusRYUKYUs", "japonicusIZU", "japonicusOGASAWARA", "japonicusHAWAII", "meyeniLANYU", "meyeniBATAN", "montanusNORTH", "montanusPALAWAN", "montanusVISAYAS", "montanusMINDANAO", "montanusINDONESIA", "simplexASIA", "simplexNA", "erythropleurus", "everetti", "nigrorum", "palpebrosus")
# Convert the factors in the data to match the desired order
ZosteropsFSTheatRO <- ZosteropsFSTheat
ZosteropsFSTheatRO$X1 <- factor(ZosteropsFSTheat$X1, levels = ZosteropsFST_reorder)
ZosteropsFSTheatRO$X2 <- factor(ZosteropsFSTheat$X2, levels = ZosteropsFST_reorder)
# Create the heatmap with ggplot
library(ggplot2)
ggplot(data = ZosteropsFSTheatRO, aes(x = X1, y = X2, fill = value)) +
  geom_tile() +  
  geom_text(aes(label = round(value, 2))) +  
  theme_minimal() +  
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "white", high = "red", space = "Lab", name = "Fst") + 
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1), axis.text.y = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))

(`geom_text()`).

Pairwise Nei’s distance heatmap

Create a heatmap of the Nei’s distance measurements for each combination of taxa/populations.

ZosteropsNeiPOP_mapping <- c("japonicusRYUKYUc", "japonicusRYUKYUs", "japonicusKOREA", "japonicusJAPAN", "japonicusOGASAWARA", "japonicusIZU", "japonicusRYUKYUn", "simplexASIA", "meyeniBATAN", "meyeniLANYU", "montanusVISAYAS", "montanusNORTH", "montanusMINDANAO", "montanusINDONESIA", "montanusPALAWAN", "nigrorum", "erythropleurus", "palpebrosus", "simplexNA", "everetti", "japonicusHAWAII")
# Reassign the X2 column with the mapped text values
ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2 <- ZosteropsNeiPOP_mapping[ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2]
ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2 <- factor(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2, levels = unique(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X1))
# Create the heatmap matrix
ggplot(data = ZosteropsNeiDheat, aes(x = X1, y = X2, fill = value))+
  geom_tile()+
  geom_text(data = ZosteropsNeiDheat, aes(label = round(value, 4)))+
  theme_minimal()+
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "white", high = "red", space = "Lab", name = "Nei's distance")+
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1), axis.text.y = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))

Create a heatmap of the pairwise Nei’s distances for each combination of taxa/populations but this time reorganize so that populations within the same taxon are kept together and they are ordered based on genetic distance.

ZosteropsNeiPOP_mapping <- c("japonicusRYUKYUc", "japonicusRYUKYUs", "japonicusKOREA", "japonicusJAPAN", "japonicusOGASAWARA", "japonicusIZU", "japonicusRYUKYUn", "simplexASIA", "meyeniBATAN", "meyeniLANYU", "montanusVISAYAS", "montanusNORTH", "montanusMINDANAO", "montanusINDONESIA", "montanusPALAWAN", "nigrorum", "erythropleurus", "palpebrosus", "simplexNA", "everetti", "japonicusHAWAII")
# Reassign the X2 column with the mapped text values
ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2 <- ZosteropsNeiPOP_mapping[ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2]
ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2 <- factor(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2, levels = unique(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X1))
# Change the order for the heatmap to match the same order for the Fst heatmap
ZosteropsFST_reorder <- c("japonicusJAPAN", "japonicusKOREA", "japonicusRYUKYUn", "japonicusRYUKYUc", "japonicusRYUKYUs", "japonicusIZU", "japonicusOGASAWARA", "japonicusHAWAII", "meyeniLANYU", "meyeniBATAN", "montanusNORTH", "montanusPALAWAN", "montanusVISAYAS", "montanusMINDANAO", "montanusINDONESIA", "simplexASIA", "simplexNA", "erythropleurus", "everetti", "nigrorum", "palpebrosus")
# Convert the factors in the data to match the desired order
ZosteropsNeiDheatRO <- ZosteropsNeiDheat
ZosteropsNeiDheatRO$X1 <- factor(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X1, levels = ZosteropsFST_reorder)
ZosteropsNeiDheatRO$X2 <- factor(ZosteropsNeiDheat$X2, levels = ZosteropsFST_reorder)
# Create the heatmap matrix
ggplot(data = ZosteropsNeiDheatRO, aes(x = X1, y = X2, fill = value))+
  geom_tile()+
  geom_text(data = ZosteropsNeiDheatRO, aes(label = round(value, 4)))+
  theme_minimal()+
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "white", high = "red", space = "Lab", name = "Nei's distance")+
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1), axis.text.y = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))

Fst map

Create a map showing the major biogeographic breaks for East Asian Zosterops and the pairwise Fst value estimated for the populations on either side of that break. In each case the Fst value was entered into the code manually from the table created in the previous step.

pac <- map_data("world")
ggplot()+
  geom_polygon(data = pac, aes(x=long, y = lat, group = group), fill="lightgrey", col="black", cex=.1)+
  coord_sf(xlim = c(116, 144.3), ylim = c(-5, 44))+
  # Biogeographic break between Minandao and Indonesia FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120, y = 4, xend = 132, yend = 6), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 133, y = 5, label = "0.22"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Visayas and Minandao FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120, y = 7, xend = 129, yend = 13), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 129.3, y = 11.4, label = "0.12"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Northern Philippines (Mindoro and Luzon) and Visayas FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120.2, y = 11.4, xend = 128, yend = 14), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 126.9, y = 14.7, label = "0.24"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Northern Philippines (Mindoro and Luzon) and Palawan FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120.2, y = 9.4, xend = 119.7, yend = 15), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 118, y = 12.5, label = "0.26"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Bantan Islands and Northen Philippines FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 119, y = 19.7, xend = 125, yend = 20), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 124.5, y = 19, label = "0.15"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Lanyu and Batan Islands FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 121.2, y = 21.2, xend = 126, yend = 21.2), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 126.9, y = 21, label = "0.08"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Southern Ryukyu Islands and Lanyu FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 123, y = 29, xend = 123.6, yend = 22), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 125.5, y = 23, label = "0.31"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between Taiwan (simplex) and Lanyu FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 122.5, y = 26, xend = 120.6, yend = 21), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 118.7, y = 23, label = "0.70"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between the central Ryukyu Islands and the Southern Ryukyu Islands FST (Hachisuka's Line)
  geom_segment(aes(x = 124.2, y = 28, xend = 129.2, yend = 22), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 130, y = 23.7, label = "0.04"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between the northern Ryukyu Islands and the central Ryukyu Islands FST (Watase's Line)
  geom_segment(aes(x = 126, y = 29.6, xend = 133, yend = 29.6), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 132.6, y = 28.5, label = "0.06"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between the main islands of Japan and the Northern Ryukyu Islands FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 127, y = 30.8, xend = 133, yend = 31.2), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 134.3, y = 31.2, label = "0.05"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between the Korean Peninsula and surrounding islands and the main islands of Japan FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 126, y = 31, xend = 131, yend = 35), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 125, y = 32.4, label = "0.02"), size = 5) +
  # Biogeographic break between the main islands of Japan and the Izu Islands FST
  geom_segment(aes(x = 136, y = 32.8, xend = 141, yend = 34.6), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 142, y = 33.6, label = "0.09"), size = 5) +

  theme_classic()

Nei’s distance map

Create a map showing the major biogeographic breaks for East Asian Zosterops and Nei’s distance estimates for the populations on either side of that break. In each case the Nei’s distance value was entered into the code manually from the table created in the previous step.

pac <- map_data("world")
ggplot()+
  geom_polygon(data = pac, aes(x=long, y = lat, group = group), fill="lightgrey", col="black", cex=.1)+
  coord_sf(xlim = c(116, 144.3), ylim = c(-5, 44))+
  # Biogeographic break between Minandao and Indonesia Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120, y = 4, xend = 132, yend = 6), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 132, y = 5, label = "0.0146"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Visayas and Minandao Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120, y = 7, xend = 129, yend = 13), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 127.9, y = 10.9, label = "0.0075"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Northern Philippines (Mindoro and Luzon) and Visayas Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120.2, y = 11.4, xend = 128, yend = 14), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 127, y = 14.5, label = "0.0137"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Northern Philippines (Mindoro and Luzon) and Palawan Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 120.2, y = 9.4, xend = 119.7, yend = 15), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 118, y = 13, label = "0.0186"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Bantan Islands and Northen Philippines Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 119, y = 19.7, xend = 125, yend = 20), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 124.5, y = 19.3, label = "0.0094"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Lanyu and Batan Islands Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 121.2, y = 21.2, xend = 126, yend = 21.2), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 127, y = 21.3, label = "0.0068"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Southern Ryukyu Islands and Lanyu Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 122, y = 29, xend = 123.6, yend = 22), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 125.1, y = 23, label = "0.014"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between Taiwan (simplex) and Lanyu Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 122.5, y = 26, xend = 120.6, yend = 21), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 118.7, y = 23, label = "0.0698"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between the central Ryukyu Islands and the Southern Ryukyu Islands Nei's distance (Hachisuka's Line)
  geom_segment(aes(x = 123.2, y = 28, xend = 129.2, yend = 22), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 129.9, y = 23.7, label = "0.0024"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between the northern Ryukyu Islands and the central Ryukyu Islands Nei's distance (Watase's Line)
  geom_segment(aes(x = 126, y = 29.8, xend = 133, yend = 29.6), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 132.6, y = 28.8, label = "0.0037"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between the main islands of Japan and the Northern Ryukyu Islands Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 127, y = 30.8, xend = 134, yend = 31.2), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 135.3, y = 31.5, label = "0.004"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between the Korean Peninsula and surrounding islands and the main islands of Japan Nei's distance
  geom_segment(aes(x = 126, y = 31, xend = 131, yend = 35), linetype = "dashed", size = 1, color = "red") +
  geom_text(aes(x = 125.5, y = 32.4, label = "0.0019"), size = 3) +
  # Biogeographic break between the main islands of Japan and the Izu Islands Nei's distance
